href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Iran%E2%80%93Saudi_Arabia_proxy_conflict#cite_note-240">[240]</a></sup> During a state visit by [Emir](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Emir_of_Qatar "Emir of Qatar") [Tamim bin Hamad Al Thani](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tamim_bin_Hamad_Al_Thani "Tamim bin Hamad Al Thani") of [Qatar](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Qatar "Qatar") to Iran, Ayatollah Khamenei called for regional cooperation against the U.S.<sup id="cite_ref-241"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Iran%E2%80%93Saudi_Arabia_proxy_conflict#cite_note-241">[241]</a></sup> However, following discussions between Sheikh Tamim and President Rouhani, Tamim concluded that de-escalation and dialogue were the only means to resolve the regional crises.<sup id="cite_ref-242"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Iran%E2%80%93Saudi_Arabia_proxy_conflict#cite_note-242">[242]</a></sup> In response to the increased tensions, the [U.S. Department of Homeland Security](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States_Department_of_Homeland_Security "United States Department of Homeland Security") and many U.S. states released advisories warning of Iranian [cyberattacks](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cyberattack "Cyberattack"), while the [Texas Department of Information Resources](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Texas_Department_of_Information_Resources "Texas Department of Information Resources") said Iranian cyberattacks had reached a rate of 10,000 per minute.<sup id="cite_ref-243"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Iran%E2%80%93Saudi_Arabia_proxy_conflict#cite_note-243">[243]</a></sup>

The 2019 Warsaw Conference would later lead to the [Abraham Accords](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Abraham_Accords "Abraham Accords"), with Saudi allies UAE and Bahrain normalizing relations with [Israel](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israel "Israel"). This was followed by [Morocco](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israel%E2%80%93Morocco_relations "Israel–Morocco relations") and [Sudan](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israel%E2%80%93Sudan_normalization_agreement "Israel–Sudan normalization agreement").<sup id="cite_ref-244"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Iran%E2%80%93Saudi_Arabia_proxy_conflict#cite_note-244">[244]</a></sup> This would later lead to the [Arab–Israeli alliance](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arab%E2%80%93Israeli_alliance "Arab–Israeli alliance"), and the [Negev Summit](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Negev_Summit "Negev Summit").<sup id="cite_ref-245"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Iran%E2%80%93Saudi_Arabia_proxy_conflict#cite_note-245">[245]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-246"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Iran%E2%80%93Saudi_Arabia_proxy_conflict#cite_note-246">[246]</a></sup> The U.S. ,<sup id="cite_ref-Tibon_60-1"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Iran%E2%80%93Saudi_Arabia_proxy_conflict#cite_note-Tibon-60">[60]</a></sup> along with Israel allegedly announced the formation of the _Middle East Air Defense Alliance_ (MEAD) in June 2022 with the purpose of countering Iran.<sup id="cite_ref-breakingdefense.com_247-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Iran%E2%80%93Saudi_Arabia_proxy_conflict#cite_note-breakingdefense.com-247">[247]</a></sup> Israel stated delegations from the U.A.E, Qatar, Bahrain, Jordan, Egypt, Saudi Arabia,<sup id="cite_ref-248"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Iran%E2%80%93Saudi_Arabia_proxy_conflict#cite_note-248">[248]</a></sup> and the U.S. participated in broker talks.<sup id="cite_ref-249"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Iran%E2%80%93Saudi_Arabia_proxy_conflict#cite_note-249">[249]</a></sup>

### 2022 [edit](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Iran%E2%80%93Saudi_Arabia_proxy_conflict&action=edit&section=16 "Edit section: 2022")

In 2022, Iran and Saudi Arabia participated in peace talks brokered by Iraq.<sup id="cite_ref-250"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Iran%E2%80%93Saudi_Arabia_proxy_conflict#cite_note-250">[250]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-251"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Iran%E2%80%93Saudi_Arabia_proxy_conflict#cite_note-251">[251]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-252"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Iran%E2%80%93Saudi_Arabia_proxy_conflict#cite_note-252">[252]</a></sup> In July of that year, the members of the [Gulf Cooperation Council](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gulf_Cooperation_Council "Gulf Cooperation Council"), alongside [Jordan](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jordan "Jordan"), [Egypt](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Egypt "Egypt"), [Iraq](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Iraq "Iraq"), and the [United States](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States "United States") participated in the Jeddah Security and Development Summit (JSDS). In the summit, members called on Iran to stop intervening in other countries' affairs, and U.S. President [Joe Biden](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Joe_Biden "Joe Biden") ensured that they will not let Iran obtain a nuclear weapon.<sup id="cite_ref-253"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Iran%E2%80%93Saudi_Arabia_proxy_conflict#cite_note-253">[253]</a></sup>

Iran has accused Saudi Arabia, the U.S., and Israel of meddling within their internal affairs due to the [Mahsa Amini protests](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mahsa_Amini_protests "Mahsa Amini protests").

In late October 2022, Saudi intelligence was shared to the U.S., warning of an imminent attack by Iran, which placed the GCC, Iraq, and Israel on high alert.<sup id="cite_ref-254"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Iran%E2%80%93Saudi_Arabia_proxy_conflict#cite_note-254">[254]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-255"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Iran%E2%80%93Saudi_Arabia_proxy_conflict#cite_note-255">[255]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-256"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Iran%E2%80%93Saudi_Arabia_proxy_conflict#cite_note-256">[256]</a></sup> The intelligence showed that Iran was allegedly planning to strike Saudi Arabia, Iraq, and the Persian Gulf. Iran denied these accusations and intel as baseless.<sup id="cite_ref-257"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Iran%E2%80%93Saudi_Arabia_proxy_conflict#cite_note-257">[257]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-258"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Iran%E2%80%93Saudi_Arabia_proxy_conflict#cite_note-258">[258]</a></sup>

## Involved parties [edit](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Iran%E2%80%93Saudi_Arabia_proxy_conflict&action=edit&section=17 "Edit section: Involved parties")

### Iranian supporters and proxies [edit](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Iran%E2%80%93Saudi_Arabia_proxy_conflict&action=edit&section=18 "Edit section: Iranian supporters and proxies")

#### Syria [edit](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Iran%E2%80%93Saudi_Arabia_proxy_conflict&action=edit&section=19 "Edit section: Syria")

 [](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Liwa_Fatemiyoun_near_Palmyra_2.png)

Iranian-supported [Liwa Fatemiyoun](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Liwa_Fatemiyoun "Liwa Fatemiyoun") fighters during the [Palmyra offensive](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Palmyra_offensive_(December_2016) "Palmyra offensive (December 2016)") in Syria in December 2016

[Syria](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Syria "Syria") under [Bashar al-Assad](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bashar_al-Assad "Bashar al-Assad") has been a strategic ally to both Iranian and Russian interests. Since 2011, the year [the civil war broke out](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Syrian_civil_war "Syrian civil war"), Iran and its allies have actively [involved themselves](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Foreign_involvement_in_the_Syrian_civil_war "Foreign involvement in the Syrian civil war") in the Syrian civil war, with many proxies.<sup id="cite_ref-259"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Iran%E2%80%93Saudi_Arabia_proxy_conflict#cite_note-259">[259]</a></sup>

Following the civil unrest triggered against the Assad regime with the [Arab uprisings](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arab_uprisings "Arab uprisings"), the main reasons for conflict in Syria were competition for regional power and sectarian divisions.<sup id="cite_ref-Mirza_Abbas_Qaisrani_2021_260-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Iran%E2%80%93Saudi_Arabia_proxy_conflict#cite_note-Mirza_Abbas_Qaisrani_2021-260">[260]</a></sup> The movement received support from Saudi Arabia, Qatar, the US and Turkey with the aim of overthrowing the Assad government. These uprisings also facilitated the influence of right-wing religious groups and parties over the movement, eventually bringing about [ISIS](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Islamic_State "Islamic State").<sup id="cite_ref-Mirza_Abbas_Qaisrani_2021_260-1"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Iran%E2%80%93Saudi_Arabia_proxy_conflict#cite_note-Mirza_Abbas_Qaisrani_2021-260">[260]</a></sup>

At the same time, Syria remained the "primary hub in Iran's power projection in the Levant" and has coordinated, and played a facilitator role over, Iran's links with [Hezbollah](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hezbollah "Hezbollah").<sup id="cite_ref-Mirza_Abbas_Qaisrani_2021_260-2"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Iran%E2%80%93Saudi_Arabia_proxy_conflict#cite_note-Mirza_Abbas_Qaisrani_2021-260">[260]</a></sup> Syria, together with Iran and Hezbollah, have been considered and defined as the "[Axis of Resistance](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Axis_of_Resistance "Axis of Resistance")" against Israel and similar competing regional states located in the [Levant](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Levant "Levant").<sup id="cite_ref-Mirza_Abbas_Qaisrani_2021_260-3"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Iran%E2%80%93Saudi_Arabia_proxy_conflict#cite_note-Mirza_Abbas_Qaisrani_2021-260">[260]</a></sup> In fact, with the intent of preserving the Assad regime, Iran sent General Qassem Suleimani, among other military commanders, providing training and assistance.<sup id="cite_ref-Mirza_Abbas_Qaisrani_2021_260-4"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Iran%E2%80%93Saudi_Arabia_proxy_conflict#cite_note-Mirza_Abbas_Qaisrani_2021-260">[260]</a></sup> The Iranian branch of the armed forces in charge of its foreign operations, i.e. the [Islamic Revolutionary Guard Corps](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Islamic_Revolutionary_Guard_Corps "Islamic Revolutionary Guard Corps") or [Quds Force](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Quds_Force "Quds Force") (IRGC-QF), intervened in the Syrian crisis by sending thousands of Iranians and by recruiting and training Shi'ites from other states.<sup id="cite_ref-:12_261-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Iran%E2%80%93Saudi_Arabia_proxy_conflict#cite_note-:12-261">[261]</a></sup> These, included [Liwa Zaynabiyoun](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Liwa_Zainebiyoun "Liwa Zainebiyoun") recruiting Pakistani Shias, and [Liwa Fatimiyoun](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Liwa_Fatemiyoun "Liwa Fatemiyoun") comprising Afghan Shi'ites.<sup id="cite_ref-:12_261-1"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Iran%E2%80%93Saudi_Arabia_proxy_conflict#cite_note-:12-261">[261]</a></sup> Iranian assistance also came under the shape of communication and intelligence monitoring technologies of the most recent type.<sup id="cite_ref-:12_261-2"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Iran%E2%80%93Saudi_Arabia_proxy_conflict#cite_note-:12-261">[261]</a></sup>

Conversely, the majority of the funding and equipment for the rebels by the Saudi state was transported through Jordan, together with the provision of ideological support.<sup id="cite_ref-:12_261-3"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Iran%E2%80%93Saudi_Arabia_proxy_conflict#cite_note-:12-261">[261]</a></sup> The rebellion was thus legitimised with the issuing by Saudi and other [Muftis](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mufti "Mufti") of _[fatwas](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fatwa "Fatwa")_ in favour of _[jihad](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jihad "Jihad")_ against the regime in Syria.<sup id="cite_ref-:12_261-4"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Iran%E2%80%93Saudi_Arabia_proxy_conflict#cite_note-:12-261">[261]</a></sup>

The long-term strategic interest of Iran in Syria was secured as the presumed victory of Bashar al-Assad and his allies against [Daesh](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Islamic_State "Islamic State") and rebel forces was declared.<sup id="cite_ref-:12_261-5"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Iran%E2%80%93Saudi_Arabia_proxy_conflict#cite_note-:12-261">[261]</a></sup>

#### Hamas [edit](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Iran%E2%80%93Saudi_Arabia_proxy_conflict&action=edit&section=20 "Edit section: Hamas")

[Hamas](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hamas "Hamas") has been allies of Iran, Hezbollah and other Iranian proxies and allies.<sup id="cite_ref-adnanabuamer_13-1"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Iran%E2%80%93Saudi_Arabia_proxy_conflict#cite_note-adnanabuamer-13">[13]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-262"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Iran%E2%80%93Saudi_Arabia_proxy_conflict#cite_note-262">[262]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-263"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Iran%E2%80%93Saudi_Arabia_proxy_conflict#cite_note-263">[263]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-264"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Iran%E2%80%93Saudi_Arabia_proxy_conflict#cite_note-264">[264]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-265"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Iran%E2%80%93Saudi_Arabia_proxy_conflict#cite_note-265">[265]</a></sup>

The organisation has received arms from Iran via [Sudan](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sudan "Sudan") that acted as "transshipment point" for their circulation, and Eritrea that allowed Iranian navy use of its ports.<sup id="cite_ref-266"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Iran%E2%80%93Saudi_Arabia_proxy_conflict#cite_note-266">[266]</a></sup>

Despite the 2005 cease fire agreement that officially ended the [Second Intifada](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Second_Intifada "Second Intifada"), friction arose as Israel attempted to gain access to the [Gaza Strip](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gaza_Strip "Gaza Strip").<sup id="cite_ref-267"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Iran%E2%80%93Saudi_Arabia_proxy_conflict#cite_note-267">[267]</a></sup> Hamas initiated a program of tunnel building to overcome the physical isolation. The history of these tunnels goes back as far as prior to the [1979 peace treaty](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Egypt%E2%80%93Israel_peace_treaty "Egypt–Israel peace treaty") between Israel and Egypt. They were used for a range of different functions: from supporting economic activity through smuggling goods, but also weapons, to infiltration into Israeli territory, abductions and attacks on Israeli soldiers.The maze of tunnels provided access to homes, mosques, schools and public buildings, according to expert in underground warfare Eado Hecht.<sup id="cite_ref-268"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Iran%E2%80%93Saudi_Arabia_proxy_conflict#cite_note-268">[268]</a></sup>

Hamas received strong rhetorical support from regime leaders [Ali Khamenei](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ali_Khamenei "Ali Khamenei"), President [Mahmoud Ahmadinejad](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mahmoud_Ahmadinejad "Mahmoud Ahmadinejad") and Majlis speaker [Ali Larijani](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ali_Larijani "Ali Larijani").<sup id="cite_ref-:13_269-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Iran%E2%80%93Saudi_Arabia_proxy_conflict#cite_note-:13-269">[269]</a></sup> In July 2008, was deemed to be part of Iran's line of defense against an Israeli attack together with Hezbollah, by [IRGC](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Islamic_Revolutionary_Guard_Corps "Islamic Revolutionary Guard Corps") chief Ali Jafari.<sup id="cite_ref-:13_269-1"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Iran%E2%80%93Saudi_Arabia_proxy_conflict#cite_note-:13-269">[269]</a></sup> Late May 2008 reports demonstrated Iran's increase in support to Hamas up to $150 million per year.<sup id="cite_ref-270"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Iran%E2%80%93Saudi_Arabia_proxy_conflict#cite_note-270">[270]</a></sup>

#### Hezbollah [edit](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Iran%E2%80%93Saudi_Arabia_proxy_conflict&action=edit&section=21 "Edit section: Hezbollah")

[Hezbollah](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hezbollah "Hezbollah") is one of the main groups in the Middle East to be described as an 'Iranian proxy'.<sup id="cite_ref-271"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Iran%E2%80%93Saudi_Arabia_proxy_conflict#cite_note-271">[271]</a></sup> Hezbollah fights alongside Iranian troops in Syria and supports the Houthis.<sup id="cite_ref-272"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Iran%E2%80%93Saudi_Arabia_proxy_conflict#cite_note-272">[272]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-273"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Iran%E2%80%93Saudi_Arabia_proxy_conflict#cite_note-273">[273]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-274"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Iran%E2%80%93Saudi_Arabia_proxy_conflict#cite_note-274">[274]</a></sup>

Hezbollah served also as inspiration to Houthis in their success at forcing the IDF out of Lebanon.<sup>[<i><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (April 2023)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup>

Iran aims to use Hezbollah as proxy model to establish throughout Africa.<sup id="cite_ref-275"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Iran%E2%80%93Saudi_Arabia_proxy_conflict#cite_note-275">[275]</a></sup> Hezbollah already possesses support in West Africa, given the large presence of Lebanese diaspora. Moreover, the group was also used by Iran in the arming and training of insurgents in Nigeria, and has been engaged in [Sierra Leone](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sierra_Leone "Sierra Leone"), [Côte d'Ivoire](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/C%C3%B4te_d%27Ivoire "Côte d'Ivoire"), and [Senegal](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Senegal "Senegal").<sup id="cite_ref-Bahi_2018_32_276-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Iran%E2%80%93Saudi_Arabia_proxy_conflict#cite_note-Bahi_2018_32-276">[276]</a></sup>

Hezbollah is often involved in the [Illegal drug trade](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Illegal_drug_trade "Illegal drug trade"),<sup id="cite_ref-277"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Iran%E2%80%93Saudi_Arabia_proxy_conflict#cite_note-277">[277]</a></sup> [terrorist activities](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Terrorism "Terrorism"),<sup id="cite_ref-278"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Iran%E2%80%93Saudi_Arabia_proxy_conflict#cite_note-278">[278]</a></sup> [proxy warfare](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Proxy_warfare "Proxy warfare"), and [sectarian violence](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sectarian_violence "Sectarian violence"). Hezbollah is funded by Iran, Syria, Qatar,<sup id="cite_ref-Weinthal_279-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Iran%E2%80%93Saudi_Arabia_proxy_conflict#cite_note-Weinthal-279">[279]</a></sup> and Iraq,<sup id="cite_ref-280"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Iran%E2%80%93Saudi_Arabia_proxy_conflict#cite_note-280">[280]</a></sup> and was formerly supported by Sudan.<sup id="cite_ref-281"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Iran%E2%80%93Saudi_Arabia_proxy_conflict#cite_note-281">[281]</a></sup> Hezbollah is also considered as a terrorist organization by the [Arab League](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arab_League "Arab League") and [GCC](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gulf_Cooperation_Council "Gulf Cooperation Council"),<sup id="cite_ref-282"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Iran%E2%80%93Saudi_Arabia_proxy_conflict#cite_note-282">[282]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-283"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Iran%E2%80%93Saudi_Arabia_proxy_conflict#cite_note-283">[283]</a></sup> as it often criticizes states like [Saudi Arabia](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Saudi_Arabia "Saudi Arabia")<sup id="cite_ref-284"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Iran%E2%80%93Saudi_Arabia_proxy_conflict#cite_note-284">[284]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-285"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Iran%E2%80%93Saudi_Arabia_proxy_conflict#cite_note-285">[285]</a></sup> and [Egypt](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Egypt "Egypt").<sup id="cite_ref-286"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Iran%E2%80%93Saudi_Arabia_proxy_conflict#cite_note-286">[286]</a></sup> Morocco has also made claims that Hezbollah funds the [Polisario Front](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Polisario_Front "Polisario Front") via Algeria.<sup id="cite_ref-287"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Iran%E2%80%93Saudi_Arabia_proxy_conflict#cite_note-287">[287]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-288"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Iran%E2%80%93Saudi_Arabia_proxy_conflict#cite_note-288">[288]</a></sup>

Hezbollah has also maintained relations with other Islamic and anti-West movements, including the [Popular Mobilization Forces](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Popular_Mobilization_Forces "Popular Mobilization Forces"),<sup id="cite_ref-cisac.fsi.stanford.edu_289-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Iran%E2%80%93Saudi_Arabia_proxy_conflict#cite_note-cisac.fsi.stanford.edu-289">[289]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-290"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Iran%E2%80%93Saudi_Arabia_proxy_conflict#cite_note-290">[290]</a></sup> [Hamas](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hamas "Hamas"),<sup id="cite_ref-291"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Iran%E2%80%93Saudi_Arabia_proxy_conflict#cite_note-291">[291]</a></sup> the [Palestinian Islamic Jihad](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Palestinian_Islamic_Jihad "Palestinian Islamic Jihad"),<sup id="cite_ref-292"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Iran%E2%80%93Saudi_Arabia_proxy_conflict#cite_note-292">[292]</a></sup><sup>[<i><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wikipedia:NOTRS" title="Wikipedia:NOTRS"><span title="This claim needs references to better sources. (October 2022)">better&nbsp;source&nbsp;needed</span></a></i>]</sup> [Al-Ashtar Brigades](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Al-Ashtar_Brigades "Al-Ashtar Brigades"), [Hezbollah Al-Hejaz](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hezbollah_Al-Hejaz "Hezbollah Al-Hejaz"), [Liwa Fatemiyoun](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Liwa_Fatemiyoun "Liwa Fatemiyoun"),<sup id="cite_ref-293"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Iran%E2%80%93Saudi_Arabia_proxy_conflict#cite_note-293">[293]</a></sup> [Husayniyun](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Husayniyun&action=edit&redlink=1 "Husayniyun (page does not exist)"), the [Houthis](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Houthis "Houthis"),<sup id="cite_ref-294"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Iran%E2%80%93Saudi_Arabia_proxy_conflict#cite_note-294">[294]</a></sup> and the [Baqir Brigade](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Baqir_Brigade "Baqir Brigade").<sup id="cite_ref-295"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Iran%E2%80%93Saudi_Arabia_proxy_conflict#cite_note-295">[295]</a></sup> These movements, among the Iranian, Syrian, and Iraqi governments, form the [Axis of Resistance](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Axis_of_Resistance "Axis of Resistance") against the [United States](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States "United States"), [Saudi Arabia](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Saudi_Arabia "Saudi Arabia"), and [Israel](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israel "Israel").<sup id="cite_ref-296"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Iran%E2%80%93Saudi_Arabia_proxy_conflict#cite_note-296">[296]</a></sup>

#### Nigerian Islamic Movement [edit](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Iran%E2%80%93Saudi_Arabia_proxy_conflict&action=edit&section=22 "Edit section: Nigerian Islamic Movement")

The [Islamic Movement of Nigeria](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Islamic_Movement_of_Nigeria "Islamic Movement of Nigeria") (IMN), a Shiite religious and political organisation founded and headed by [Sheikh Ibrahim Zakzaki](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ibrahim_Zakzaky "Ibrahim Zakzaky"), constitutes another proxy in the conflict. It constitutes another asset that could enable Iran in disrupting Sunni States in West Africa.<sup id="cite_ref-Bahi_2018_32_276-1"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Iran%E2%80%93Saudi_Arabia_proxy_conflict#cite_note-Bahi_2018_32-276">[276]</a></sup> Thus, Saudi Arabia by supporting the Nigerian government in its suppressing efforts, and by providing support to rival Sunni groups such as [Izala](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Izala_Society "Izala Society") and not seriously condemning Boko Haram's actions, aims to limit its influence and growth in the region.<sup id="cite_ref-Bahi_2018_33_19-1"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Iran%E2%80%93Saudi_Arabia_proxy_conflict#cite_note-Bahi_2018_33-19">[19]</a></sup>

#### Houthis [edit](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Iran%E2%80%93Saudi_Arabia_proxy_conflict&action=edit&section=23 "Edit section: Houthis")

Iran and its allies North Korea, Syria, Iraq, Qatar, Hezbollah, and Venezuela are known to have provided political, economical, diplomatic, and military support to the Houthis<sup id="cite_ref-297"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Iran%E2%80%93Saudi_Arabia_proxy_conflict#cite_note-297">[297]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-298"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Iran%E2%80%93Saudi_Arabia_proxy_conflict#cite_note-298">[298]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-299"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Iran%E2%80%93Saudi_Arabia_proxy_conflict#cite_note-299">[299]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-300"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Iran%E2%80%93Saudi_Arabia_proxy_conflict#cite_note-300">[300]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-301"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Iran%E2%80%93Saudi_Arabia_proxy_conflict#cite_note-301">[301]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-302"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Iran%E2%80%93Saudi_Arabia_proxy_conflict#cite_note-302">[302]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-303"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Iran%E2%80%93Saudi_Arabia_proxy_conflict#cite_note-303">[303]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Yobserver_2011-09-04_37-1"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Iran%E2%80%93Saudi_Arabia_proxy_conflict#cite_note-Yobserver_2011-09-04-37">[37]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-304"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Iran%E2%80%93Saudi_Arabia_proxy_conflict#cite_note-304">[304]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-305"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Iran%E2%80%93Saudi_Arabia_proxy_conflict#cite_note-305">[305]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-306"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Iran%E2%80%93Saudi_Arabia_proxy_conflict#cite_note-306">[306]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-307"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Iran%E2%80%93Saudi_Arabia_proxy_conflict#cite_note-307">[307]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-308"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Iran%E2%80%93Saudi_Arabia_proxy_conflict#cite_note-308">[308]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-309"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Iran%E2%80%93Saudi_Arabia_proxy_conflict#cite_note-309">[309]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-310"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Iran%E2%80%93Saudi_Arabia_proxy_conflict#cite_note-310">[310]</a></sup>

Houthis overthrew the government in Yemen in the [September 21 Revolution](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Houthi_takeover_in_Yemen "Houthi takeover in Yemen") or 2014–15 coup d'état, supported by Iran while Saudi Arabia was attempting to restore the central government through a military campaign.<sup id="cite_ref-311"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Iran%E2%80%93Saudi_Arabia_proxy_conflict#cite_note-311">[311]</a></sup> Since the uprising, they have evolved into a well-organised and equipped militia in Yemen.<sup id="cite_ref-Mirza_Abbas_Qaisrani_2021_260-5"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Iran%E2%80%93Saudi_Arabia_proxy_conflict#cite_note-Mirza_Abbas_Qaisrani_2021-260">[260]</a></sup>

Houthis can be considered to be similar in their response to Hamas, rather than Hezbollah, given the varying degrees of resources and support without actually responding to or informing Iran.<sup id="cite_ref-312"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Iran%E2%80%93Saudi_Arabia_proxy_conflict#cite_note-312">[312]</a></sup> In fact, Houthis took control of Sanaa in September 2014, despite Iran's advising restraint.<sup id="cite_ref-313"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Iran%E2%80%93Saudi_Arabia_proxy_conflict#cite_note-313">[313]</a></sup> Saudi officials believe Houthis will become the "next Hezbollah" that operates close to Saudi territory.<sup id="cite_ref-314"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Iran%E2%80%93Saudi_Arabia_proxy_conflict#cite_note-314">[314]</a></sup> Moreover, Houthis have been supported in their fight against the Yemeni government through a gateway for arms and supplies smuggling from Iran through Somalia since 2015.<sup id="cite_ref-Bahi_2018_30_315-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Iran%E2%80%93Saudi_Arabia_proxy_conflict#cite_note-Bahi_2018_30-315">[315]</a></sup> Access to Somalia, as well as to Eritrea, together with control of Yemen's Red Sea coast through the Houthis, provided Iran's with an enhanced ability to threaten international shipping in the [Bab al-Mandeb](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bab-el-Mandeb "Bab-el-Mandeb"). An instances of this capacity was constituted by the several attacks on U.S. and coalition vessels that were set in motion from the Yemeni side of the Bab al-Mandeb in 2016.<sup id="cite_ref-Bahi_2018_30_315-1"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Iran%E2%80%93Saudi_Arabia_proxy_conflict#cite_note-Bahi_2018_30-315">[315]</a></sup>

A military campaign against Houthis was started by a Saudi-led coalition on the request of ousted [President Mansur](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Abdrabbuh_Mansur_Hadi "Abdrabbuh Mansur Hadi"), dividing the state between pro-Houthi forces supported by Iran and pro-Mansur forces supported by Saudi Arabia.<sup id="cite_ref-Mirza_Abbas_Qaisrani_2021_260-6"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Iran%E2%80%93Saudi_Arabia_proxy_conflict#cite_note-Mirza_Abbas_Qaisrani_2021-260">[260]</a></sup> The competition between the two countries has exacerbated the suffering of the Yemeni population, the half of which is deemed to be facing a "pre-famine condition", as reported by the UN in 2018.

In 2022, multiple events occurred, including the following:

-   On March 16, 2022, Yemen's Houthi rebels said that negotiations with the Saudi-led coalition would be welcome if the site was a neutral country, such as the Gulf states, and that the top goal would be to relieve "arbitrary" restrictions on Yemeni ports and [Sanaa airport](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sanaa_International_Airport "Sanaa International Airport").<sup id="cite_ref-316"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Iran%E2%80%93Saudi_Arabia_proxy_conflict#cite_note-316">[316]</a></sup>
-   On March 20, 2022, according to the Saudi energy ministry and official media, Yemen's Iran-aligned Houthi militia fired missiles and drones against Saudi energy and water desalination facilities, causing a short dip in output at a refinery but no injuries.<sup id="cite_ref-317"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Iran%E2%80%93Saudi_Arabia_proxy_conflict#cite_note-317">[317]</a></sup>
-   On March 26, 2022, the Saudi-led coalition in Yemen gave the Iran-aligned Houthis a three-hour ultimatum to withdraw weaponry from Sanaa's airport and the two Red Sea ports.<sup id="cite_ref-318"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Iran%E2%80%93Saudi_Arabia_proxy_conflict#cite_note-318">[318]</a></sup>
-   On April 1, 2022, the warring parties in Yemen's seven-year conflict have agreed to a statewide truce for the first time in years, allowing fuel imports into Houthi-held areas and certain planes to operate from [Sanaa airport](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sanaa_International_Airport "Sanaa International Airport").<sup id="cite_ref-319"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Iran%E2%80%93Saudi_Arabia_proxy_conflict#cite_note-319">[319]</a></sup>
-   On April 13, 2022, the [US Navy](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States_Navy "United States Navy") announced the formation of a new multinational task force to target arms smuggling in Yemeni waterways, being the latest American military response to Houthi attacks on Saudi Arabia and the UAE.<sup id="cite_ref-320"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Iran%E2%80%93Saudi_Arabia_proxy_conflict#cite_note-320">[320]</a></sup>
-   On April 28, 2022, as part of a humanitarian move, the Saudi-led coalition fighting in Yemen said that it would release 163 prisoners from Yemen's Iran-aligned Houthi militia who fought against the kingdom.<sup id="cite_ref-321"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Iran%E2%80%93Saudi_Arabia_proxy_conflict#cite_note-321">[321]</a></sup>
-   On May 6, 2022, the Saudi-led coalition in Yemen said on Friday it transported more than 100 freed inmates to Yemen in conjunction with the [International Committee of the Red Cross](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/International_Committee_of_the_Red_Cross "International Committee of the Red Cross").<sup id="cite_ref-322"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Iran%E2%80%93Saudi_Arabia_proxy_conflict#cite_note-322">[322]</a></sup>
-   On May 12, 2022, three officials stated that Yemen's government has agreed to enable Houthi-issued passport holders to travel outside the country.<sup id="cite_ref-323"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Iran%E2%80%93Saudi_Arabia_proxy_conflict#cite_note-323">[323]</a></sup>
-   On June 2, 2022, Yemen's warring sides agreed to extend a U.N.-brokered truce for another two months on the same terms as the previous agreement, which was set to expire on June 2, according to the United Nations envoy to Yemen.<sup id="cite_ref-324"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Iran%E2%80%93Saudi_Arabia_proxy_conflict#cite_note-324">[324]</a></sup>

In April 2023, Saudi Arabia had freed more than a dozen Houthi detainees ahead of a wider prisoner release agreed upon by the warring sides. The deal was brokered by [Oman](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Oman "Oman") and will include future releases of more Houthi prisoners in an effort to normalize political and economic relations in the region.<sup id="cite_ref-325"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Iran%E2%80%93Saudi_Arabia_proxy_conflict#cite_note-325">[325]</a></sup>

#### Iraqi militias [edit](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Iran%E2%80%93Saudi_Arabia_proxy_conflict&action=edit&section=24 "Edit section: Iraqi militias")

Various [Iraqi groups](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Private_militias_in_Iraq "Private militias in Iraq"), many of them as part of the [Popular Mobilization Forces](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Popular_Mobilization_Forces "Popular Mobilization Forces"), have been described as Iranian proxies.<sup id="cite_ref-326"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Iran%E2%80%93Saudi_Arabia_proxy_conflict#cite_note-326">[326]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-327"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Iran%E2%80%93Saudi_Arabia_proxy_conflict#cite_note-327">[327]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-csis_328-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Iran%E2%80%93Saudi_Arabia_proxy_conflict#cite_note-csis-328">[328]</a></sup>

During the [Iraqi insurgency](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Iraqi_insurgency_(2003%E2%80%932011) "Iraqi insurgency (2003–2011)"), Iran aided Shi'ite groups such as the [Mahdi army](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mahdi_army "Mahdi army") while private Saudi citizens and the Saudi government aided anti-Iran and Sunni militias.<sup id="cite_ref-329"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Iran%E2%80%93Saudi_Arabia_proxy_conflict#cite_note-329">[329]</a></sup> Saudi Arabia supported the [2012–2013 Iraqi protests](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012%E2%80%932013_Iraqi_protests "2012–2013 Iraqi protests"), and the [2019–2021 Iraqi protests](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/2019%E2%80%932021_Iraqi_protests "2019–2021 Iraqi protests"),<sup id="cite_ref-330"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Iran%E2%80%93Saudi_Arabia_proxy_conflict#cite_note-330">[330]</a></sup> in which protesters protested against Shi'ite prime ministers [Nouri al-Maliki](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nouri_al-Maliki "Nouri al-Maliki") and [Adil Abdul-Mahdi](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Adil_Abdul-Mahdi "Adil Abdul-Mahdi"), respectively.

The Popular Mobilization Forces rose to prominence in 2014 when Shia groups banded together during the [Iraq-ISIL War](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Iraq-ISIL_War "Iraq-ISIL War"). The PMF, aided by Iran and [Syria](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Syria "Syria") and supported internally by al-Maliki and [Haider al-Abadi](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Haider_al-Abadi "Haider al-Abadi"), [defeated ISIL](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/2017_Western_Iraq_campaign "2017 Western Iraq campaign") internally by December 2017, however, refused to disarm, and waged attacks against [American forces](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States_Armed_Forces "United States Armed Forces") in Syria and Iraq. These groups also supported other 'Islamic Resistance Movements' such as [Hezbollah](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hezbollah "Hezbollah"),<sup id="cite_ref-331"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Iran%E2%80%93Saudi_Arabia_proxy_conflict#cite_note-331">[331]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-cisac.fsi.stanford.edu_289-1"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Iran%E2%80%93Saudi_Arabia_proxy_conflict#cite_note-cisac.fsi.stanford.edu-289">[289]</a></sup> [Hamas](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hamas "Hamas"), [Al-Mukhtar Brigades](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Al-Mukhtar_Brigades "Al-Mukhtar Brigades"), the [Houthi movement](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Houthi_movement "Houthi movement"),<sup id="cite_ref-332"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Iran%E2%80%93Saudi_Arabia_proxy_conflict#cite_note-332">[332]</a></sup> the [Palestinian Islamic Jihad](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Palestinian_Islamic_Jihad "Palestinian Islamic Jihad"), and [Hezbollah Al-Hejaz](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hezbollah_Al-Hejaz "Hezbollah Al-Hejaz"),<sup id="cite_ref-333"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Iran%E2%80%93Saudi_Arabia_proxy_conflict#cite_note-333">[333]</a></sup> as part of the [Axis of Resistance](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Axis_of_Resistance "Axis of Resistance"). The PMF also engaged in the 2019–2021 Persian Gulf crisis against CJTF-OIR.

#### Bahraini militias [edit](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Iran%E2%80%93Saudi_Arabia_proxy_conflict&action=edit&section=25 "Edit section: Bahraini militias")

Iran and its allies have backed multiple Shia groups in Bahrain. These opposition groups include:

-   [Al-Ashtar Brigades](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Al-Ashtar_Brigades "Al-Ashtar Brigades")
-   [Al-Mukhtar Brigades](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Al-Mukhtar_Brigades "Al-Mukhtar Brigades")
-   [Waad Allah Brigades](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Waad_Allah_Brigades "Waad Allah Brigades")
-   [Saraya Thair Allah](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Saraya_Thair_Allah&action=edit&redlink=1 "Saraya Thair Allah (page does not exist)")
-   [Popular Resistance Brigades](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Popular_Resistance_Brigades&action=edit&redlink=1 "Popular Resistance Brigades (page does not exist)")
-   [February 14 Youth Coalition](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/February_14_Youth_Coalition "February 14 Youth Coalition")
-   Other minor groups

These groups fight the Bahraini government in order to overthrow the [House of Khalifa](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/House_of_Khalifa "House of Khalifa"). These groups are backed by Iran and [Kata'ib Hezbollah](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kata%27ib_Hezbollah "Kata'ib Hezbollah") financially, militarily, verbally, and ideologically.<sup id="cite_ref-334"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Iran%E2%80%93Saudi_Arabia_proxy_conflict#cite_note-334">[334]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-335"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Iran%E2%80%93Saudi_Arabia_proxy_conflict#cite_note-335">[335]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-336"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Iran%E2%80%93Saudi_Arabia_proxy_conflict#cite_note-336">[336]</a></sup> These groups, in turn, support Iran and the [Axis of Resistance](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Axis_of_Resistance "Axis of Resistance") in conflicts in Syria, Palestine, and Iraq. Exceptionally, the February 14 Youth Coalition, founded during the [2011 Bahraini uprising](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/2011_Bahraini_uprising "2011 Bahraini uprising"), became a paramilitary group during the Shia insurgency.<sup id="cite_ref-337"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Iran%E2%80%93Saudi_Arabia_proxy_conflict#cite_note-337">[337]</a></sup>

### Saudi Arabian supporters and proxies [edit](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Iran%E2%80%93Saudi_Arabia_proxy_conflict&action=edit&section=26 "Edit section: Saudi Arabian supporters and proxies")

#### Gulf Cooperation Council [edit](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Iran%E2%80%93Saudi_Arabia_proxy_conflict&action=edit&section=27 "Edit section: Gulf Cooperation Council")

The [Gulf Cooperation Council](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gulf_Cooperation_Council "Gulf Cooperation Council"), an alliance of Sunni Arab States of the Gulf region including Saudi Arabia, has often been described as a Saudi headed alliance to counter Iran, which engaged pro-Saudi interests in Bahrain.<sup id="cite_ref-Human_Rights_Watch_338-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Iran%E2%80%93Saudi_Arabia_proxy_conflict#cite_note-Human_Rights_Watch-338">[338]</a></sup>

##### Bahrain [edit](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Iran%E2%80%93Saudi_Arabia_proxy_conflict&action=edit&section=28 "Edit section: Bahrain")

[Bahrain](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bahrain "Bahrain") is a major ally to Saudi interests, and a major member of the [Gulf Cooperation Council](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gulf_Cooperation_Council "Gulf Cooperation Council"). Bahrain is a member of the [Saudi coalition](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Saudi-led_intervention_in_Yemen "Saudi-led intervention in Yemen") against the [Houthis](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Houthis "Houthis"). However, Bahrain's population is somewhere between 70 and 85% [Shia](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Shia_Islam "Shia Islam"), and has led to protests, of which, the most notable was the [2011 protests](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/2011_Bahraini_protests "2011 Bahraini protests"), which were suppressed by the [Peninsular Shield Force](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Peninsula_Shield_Force "Peninsula Shield Force").<sup id="cite_ref-339"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Iran%E2%80%93Saudi_Arabia_proxy_conflict#cite_note-339">[339]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-340"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Iran%E2%80%93Saudi_Arabia_proxy_conflict#cite_note-340">[340]</a></sup>

Iran has been accused of supporting militant groups in the [insurgency in Bahrain](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Insurgency_in_Bahrain "Insurgency in Bahrain"), especially the [Al-Ashtar Brigades](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Al-Ashtar_Brigades "Al-Ashtar Brigades").<sup id="cite_ref-341"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Iran%E2%80%93Saudi_Arabia_proxy_conflict#cite_note-341">[341]</a></sup> Iran also formerly supported the [Islamic Front for the Liberation of Bahrain](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Islamic_Front_for_the_Liberation_of_Bahrain "Islamic Front for the Liberation of Bahrain") in attempting to overthrow the Bahraini monarchy, as such [in 1981](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/1981_Bahraini_coup_d%27%C3%A9tat_attempt "1981 Bahraini coup d'état attempt").<sup id="cite_ref-342"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Iran%E2%80%93Saudi_Arabia_proxy_conflict#cite_note-342">[342]</a></sup>

Bahrain has also historically on the Saudi side, as it sent weapons to Iraq during the [Iran–Iraq War](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Iran%E2%80%93Iraq_War "Iran–Iraq War"),<sup id="cite_ref-343"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Iran%E2%80%93Saudi_Arabia_proxy_conflict#cite_note-343">[343]</a></sup> aided the [Syrian opposition](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Syrian_opposition "Syrian opposition"),<sup id="cite_ref-344"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Iran%E2%80%93Saudi_Arabia_proxy_conflict#cite_note-344">[344]</a></sup> sent troops to the [Saudi Arabian–led coalition in Yemen](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Saudi_Arabian%E2%80%93led_intervention_in_Yemen "Saudi Arabian–led intervention in Yemen"),<sup id="cite_ref-345"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Iran%E2%80%93Saudi_Arabia_proxy_conflict#cite_note-345">[345]</a></sup> severed ties with Iran in the aftermath of the [2016 attack on the Saudi diplomatic missions in Iran](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/2016_attack_on_the_Saudi_diplomatic_missions_in_Iran "2016 attack on the Saudi diplomatic missions in Iran"),<sup id="cite_ref-Saudi_allies_346-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Iran%E2%80%93Saudi_Arabia_proxy_conflict#cite_note-Saudi_allies-346">[346]</a></sup> and signed the [Abraham Accords](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Abraham_Accords "Abraham Accords") in 2020 with Israel.<sup id="cite_ref-347"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Iran%E2%80%93Saudi_Arabia_proxy_conflict#cite_note-347">[347]</a></sup>

##### Kuwait [edit](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Iran%E2%80%93Saudi_Arabia_proxy_conflict&action=edit&section=29 "Edit section: Kuwait")

[Kuwait](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kuwait "Kuwait") is a strategic ally to Saudi interests in the Gulf area. Kuwait has involved itself in [the Yemeni Civil War](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Saudi_Arabian%E2%80%93led_intervention_in_Yemen "Saudi Arabian–led intervention in Yemen") as part of the Saudi coalition,<sup id="cite_ref-348"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Iran%E2%80%93Saudi_Arabia_proxy_conflict#cite_note-348">[348]</a></sup> along with formerly supporting the [Syrian opposition](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Syrian_opposition "Syrian opposition").<sup id="cite_ref-349"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Iran%E2%80%93Saudi_Arabia_proxy_conflict#cite_note-349">[349]</a></sup>

##### United Arab Emirates [edit](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Iran%E2%80%93Saudi_Arabia_proxy_conflict&action=edit&section=30 "Edit section: United Arab Emirates")

The U.A.E and Saudi Arabia are strategic allies, as both see Iran as a common enemy.<sup id="cite_ref-350"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Iran%E2%80%93Saudi_Arabia_proxy_conflict#cite_note-350">[350]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-351"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Iran%E2%80%93Saudi_Arabia_proxy_conflict#cite_note-351">[351]</a></sup>

The U.A.E has been a major contributor to the [Saudi Arabian–led coalition in Yemen](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Saudi_Arabian%E2%80%93led_intervention_in_Yemen "Saudi Arabian–led intervention in Yemen"),<sup id="cite_ref-352"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Iran%E2%80%93Saudi_Arabia_proxy_conflict#cite_note-352">[352]</a></sup> has supported the [Autonomous Administration of North and East Syria](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Autonomous_Administration_of_North_and_East_Syria "Autonomous Administration of North and East Syria"), and joined up with Saudi Arabia and Egypt to support the [Libyan National Army](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Libyan_National_Army "Libyan National Army") and its leader [Khalifa Haftar](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Khalifa_Haftar "Khalifa Haftar").<sup id="cite_ref-353"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Iran%E2%80%93Saudi_Arabia_proxy_conflict#cite_note-353">[353]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-354"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Iran%E2%80%93Saudi_Arabia_proxy_conflict#cite_note-354">[354]</a></sup>

#### Kurdish insurgents [edit](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Iran%E2%80%93Saudi_Arabia_proxy_conflict&action=edit&section=31 "Edit section: Kurdish insurgents")

Saudi Arabia has allegedly provided support to the Kurdish militants within the [KDPI](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Democratic_Party_of_Iranian_Kurdistan "Democratic Party of Iranian Kurdistan"), [PAK](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kurdistan_Freedom_Party "Kurdistan Freedom Party"), and [PJAK](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kurdistan_Free_Life_Party "Kurdistan Free Life Party") through its consulate in [Erbil](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Erbil "Erbil"), the capital of the [Kurdistan Regional Government](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kurdistan_Regional_Government "Kurdistan Regional Government") in [Iraqi Kurdistan](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Iraqi_Kurdistan "Iraqi Kurdistan").<sup id="cite_ref-355"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Iran%E2%80%93Saudi_Arabia_proxy_conflict#cite_note-355">[355]</a></sup> Saudi Arabia and the UAE has also supported the Kurdish-led [Autonomous Administration of North and East Syria](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Autonomous_Administration_of_North_and_East_Syria "Autonomous Administration of North and East Syria"), as part of [CJTF-OIR](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/CJTF-OIR "CJTF-OIR").<sup id="cite_ref-uaesaud_356-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Iran%E2%80%93Saudi_Arabia_proxy_conflict#cite_note-uaesaud-356">[356]</a></sup> Saudi Arabia also support Iraqi Kurdistan against Iraq and Iran.<sup id="cite_ref-Ibish_357-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Iran%E2%80%93Saudi_Arabia_proxy_conflict#cite_note-Ibish-357">[357]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-economist.com_358-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Iran%E2%80%93Saudi_Arabia_proxy_conflict#cite_note-economist.com-358">[358]</a></sup>

#### Albania [edit](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Iran%E2%80%93Saudi_Arabia_proxy_conflict&action=edit&section=32 "Edit section: Albania")

Due to Albania's decision to welcome the [MEK](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/People%27s_Mojahedin_Organization_of_Iran "People's Mojahedin Organization of Iran") to take refuge in the country, tensions between Iran and Albania increased. Since 2018, Albania has accused Iran of hounding Iranian dissidents and has expelled several Iranian diplomats.<sup id="cite_ref-359"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Iran%E2%80%93Saudi_Arabia_proxy_conflict#cite_note-359">[359]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-360"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Iran%E2%80%93Saudi_Arabia_proxy_conflict#cite_note-360">[360]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-361"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Iran%E2%80%93Saudi_Arabia_proxy_conflict#cite_note-361">[361]</a></sup> In January 2020, following the death of [Qasem Soleimani](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Qasem_Soleimani "Qasem Soleimani"), the Iranian government lashed out at Albania for hosting MEK members, and Iran has increased cyberattacks and agent hunting on Iranian dissidents against Albania.<sup id="cite_ref-Deutsche_Welle_2020-01-21_362-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Iran%E2%80%93Saudi_Arabia_proxy_conflict#cite_note-Deutsche_Welle_2020-01-21-362">[362]</a></sup> Saudi Arabia, in response, announced its support for Albania in its efforts against Iran.<sup id="cite_ref-363"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Iran%E2%80%93Saudi_Arabia_proxy_conflict#cite_note-363">[363]</a></sup>

#### Jaish ul-Adl [edit](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Iran%E2%80%93Saudi_Arabia_proxy_conflict&action=edit&section=33 "Edit section: Jaish ul-Adl")

The rebel group [Jaish ul-Adl](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jaish_ul-Adl "Jaish ul-Adl"), active in the [Sistan and Baluchestan](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sistan_and_Baluchestan_Province "Sistan and Baluchestan Province") region of Iran, is accused by Iranian authorities of receiving Saudi and American support.<sup id="cite_ref-Telegraph_2014-03-28_43-1"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Iran%E2%80%93Saudi_Arabia_proxy_conflict#cite_note-Telegraph_2014-03-28-43">[43]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-364"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Iran%E2%80%93Saudi_Arabia_proxy_conflict#cite_note-364">[364]</a></sup>

#### Israel [edit](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Iran%E2%80%93Saudi_Arabia_proxy_conflict&action=edit&section=34 "Edit section: Israel")

The speaker of Iran's parliament, [Ali Larijani](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ali_Larijani "Ali Larijani"), stated that Saudi Arabia gave "strategic" intelligence information to Israel during the [2006 Lebanon War](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/2006_Lebanon_War "2006 Lebanon War").<sup id="cite_ref-365"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Iran%E2%80%93Saudi_Arabia_proxy_conflict#cite_note-365">[365]</a></sup> In May 2018, Israeli defense minister [Avigdor Lieberman](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Avigdor_Lieberman "Avigdor Lieberman") supported greater discussion between Israel, Saudi Arabia and the Gulf states, stating "It's time for the Middle East to \[...\] have an axis of moderate countries," opposed to the network of Iranian allies and proxies.<sup id="cite_ref-nyt_13-05-2018_216-1"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Iran%E2%80%93Saudi_Arabia_proxy_conflict#cite_note-nyt_13-05-2018-216">[216]</a></sup> As of 2018, several sources described alleged intelligence ties between Saudi Arabia and Israel as a "covert alliance", with a joint interest to counter Iran in the region.<sup id="cite_ref-366"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Iran%E2%80%93Saudi_Arabia_proxy_conflict#cite_note-366">[366]</a></sup> [The New York Times](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/The_New_York_Times "The New York Times") remarked that such cooperation was made more difficult by controversy over Israel's attitude towards Palestinians.<sup id="cite_ref-367"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Iran%E2%80%93Saudi_Arabia_proxy_conflict#cite_note-367">[367]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-368"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Iran%E2%80%93Saudi_Arabia_proxy_conflict#cite_note-368">[368]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-369"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Iran%E2%80%93Saudi_Arabia_proxy_conflict#cite_note-369">[369]</a></sup>

Israel and Saudi Arabia are both part of the Middle East Air Defense Alliance (MEAD).<sup id="cite_ref-breakingdefense.com_247-1"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Iran%E2%80%93Saudi_Arabia_proxy_conflict#cite_note-breakingdefense.com-247">[247]</a></sup>

#### United States [edit](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Iran%E2%80%93Saudi_Arabia_proxy_conflict&action=edit&section=35 "Edit section: United States")

The United States and Saudi Arabia have a strategic relationship that dates back to 1947.<sup id="cite_ref-370"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Iran%E2%80%93Saudi_Arabia_proxy_conflict#cite_note-370">[370]</a></sup>

When the [Iranian Revolution](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Iranian_Revolution "Iranian Revolution") occurred, revolutionaries began to [support other uprisings and rebellions](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Exporting_the_revolution "Exporting the revolution") throughout the [Muslim world](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Muslim_world "Muslim world"), including in [Bahrain](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/1981_Bahraini_coup_d%27%C3%A9tat_attempt "1981 Bahraini coup d'état attempt") and [Saudi Arabia](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Qatif_conflict "Qatif conflict"). Iran used [this policy](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/The_policy_of_exporting_the_Islamic_Revolution "The policy of exporting the Islamic Revolution") to undermine their sovereignty while fighting in proxy warfare.<sup id="cite_ref-371"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Iran%E2%80%93Saudi_Arabia_proxy_conflict#cite_note-371">[371]</a></sup> This caused Saudi Arabia and the other Gulf allies to turn to the U.S. for support.

The U.S., Saudi Arabia, and the [GCC](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gulf_Cooperation_Council "Gulf Cooperation Council") jointly backed [Iraq](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ba%27athist_Iraq "Ba'athist Iraq") under [Saddam Hussein](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Saddam_Hussein "Saddam Hussein") during the [Iran–Iraq War](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Iran%E2%80%93Iraq_War "Iran–Iraq War") and the U.S. and Iran directly attacked each other during the [Tanker War](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tanker_War "Tanker War").<sup id="cite_ref-372"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Iran%E2%80%93Saudi_Arabia_proxy_conflict#cite_note-372">[372]</a></sup>

The U.S. and Iran again opened in mistrust during the [Iraq War](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Iraq_War "Iraq War"), with the U.S. and the GCC accusing Iran of funding and militarizing its proxies and Shia groups within Iraq.<sup id="cite_ref-373"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Iran%E2%80%93Saudi_Arabia_proxy_conflict#cite_note-373">[373]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-374"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Iran%E2%80%93Saudi_Arabia_proxy_conflict#cite_note-374">[374]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-375"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Iran%E2%80%93Saudi_Arabia_proxy_conflict#cite_note-375">[375]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-376"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Iran%E2%80%93Saudi_Arabia_proxy_conflict#cite_note-376">[376]</a></sup> The highest point of mutual distrust happened in 2005 after details of [Iran's nuclear program](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nuclear_program_of_Iran "Nuclear program of Iran") were leaked, and sanctions by the UN were put in place.<sup id="cite_ref-377"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Iran%E2%80%93Saudi_Arabia_proxy_conflict#cite_note-377">[377]</a></sup> The sanctions were put in place until 2015, when the [JCPOA](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/JCPOA "JCPOA") was implemented.

Iran and U.S. have also been embroiled in tensions due to the wars in [Syria](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Syrian_civil_war "Syrian civil war"),<sup id="cite_ref-378"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Iran%E2%80%93Saudi_Arabia_proxy_conflict#cite_note-378">[378]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-379"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Iran%E2%80%93Saudi_Arabia_proxy_conflict#cite_note-379">[379]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-380"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Iran%E2%80%93Saudi_Arabia_proxy_conflict#cite_note-380">[380]</a></sup> [Afghanistan](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/War_in_Afghanistan_(2001%E2%80%932021) "War in Afghanistan (2001–2021)"),<sup id="cite_ref-381"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Iran%E2%80%93Saudi_Arabia_proxy_conflict#cite_note-381">[381]</a></sup> [Iraq](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Iraqi_conflict_(2003%E2%80%93present) "Iraqi conflict (2003–present)"),<sup id="cite_ref-382"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Iran%E2%80%93Saudi_Arabia_proxy_conflict#cite_note-382">[382]</a></sup> and disputes surrounding the [Strait of Hormuz](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Strait_of_Hormuz "Strait of Hormuz").<sup id="cite_ref-383"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Iran%E2%80%93Saudi_Arabia_proxy_conflict#cite_note-383">[383]</a></sup> In the [2011–2012 Strait of Hormuz dispute](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/2011%E2%80%932012_Strait_of_Hormuz_dispute "2011–2012 Strait of Hormuz dispute"), Iran threatened to close Hormuz, however, was forced to back down after the [EU](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/EU "EU") placed sanctions.<sup id="cite_ref-384"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Iran%E2%80%93Saudi_Arabia_proxy_conflict#cite_note-384">[384]</a></sup>

The U.S. and Iran were brought to the brink of war during the 2019–2021 Persian Gulf crisis, when the U.S. [assassinated](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Assassination_of_Qasem_Soleimani "Assassination of Qasem Soleimani") [Qasem Soleimani](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Qasem_Soleimani "Qasem Soleimani") and [Abu Mahdi al-Muhandis](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Abu_Mahdi_al-Muhandis "Abu Mahdi al-Muhandis"), leaders of the [Quds Force](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Quds_Force "Quds Force") and the [Popular Mobilization Forces](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Popular_Mobilization_Forces "Popular Mobilization Forces"), respectively. This was after the [December 2019 United States airstrikes in Iraq and Syria](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/December_2019_United_States_airstrikes_in_Iraq_and_Syria "December 2019 United States airstrikes in Iraq and Syria") and the [Attack on the United States embassy in Baghdad](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Attack_on_the_United_States_embassy_in_Baghdad "Attack on the United States embassy in Baghdad"), and Iran retaliated by [bombing](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Operation_Martyr_Soleimani "Operation Martyr Soleimani") [Al Asad Airbase](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Al_Asad_Airbase "Al Asad Airbase") in Iraq.<sup id="cite_ref-385"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Iran%E2%80%93Saudi_Arabia_proxy_conflict#cite_note-385">[385]</a></sup>

U.S.-Saudi relations have deteriorated due to the [Yemeni civil war](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Yemeni_Civil_War_(2014%E2%80%93present) "Yemeni Civil War (2014–present)") and [Syrian civil war](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Syrian_civil_war "Syrian civil war"). Saudi Arabia formerly supported the [Al-Nusra Front](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Al-Nusra_Front "Al-Nusra Front"), an [Al-Qaeda](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Al-Qaeda "Al-Qaeda") affiliate in Syria.<sup id="cite_ref-Turkeyy-KSA_386-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Iran%E2%80%93Saudi_Arabia_proxy_conflict#cite_note-Turkeyy-KSA-386">[386]</a></sup> Saudi Arabia has also been [involved in war crimes](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/War_crimes_in_the_Yemeni_Civil_War_(2014-present) "War crimes in the Yemeni Civil War (2014-present)") in Yemen due to civilian airstrikes and a humanitarian blockade.<sup id="cite_ref-387"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Iran%E2%80%93Saudi_Arabia_proxy_conflict#cite_note-387">[387]</a></sup> The U.S. supported the [Saudi Arabian–led invasion](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Saudi_Arabian%E2%80%93led_intervention_in_Yemen "Saudi Arabian–led intervention in Yemen") until 2022, when [Joe Biden](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Joe_Biden "Joe Biden") repealed support for it and halted arm sales to Saudi Arabia and the U.A.E.<sup id="cite_ref-388"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Iran%E2%80%93Saudi_Arabia_proxy_conflict#cite_note-388">[388]</a></sup>

US Secretary of State [Mike Pompeo](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mike_Pompeo "Mike Pompeo") denounced the [attacks on the Saudi oil industry](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/2019_Abqaiq%E2%80%93Khurais_attack "2019 Abqaiq–Khurais attack"), on 14 September 2019, as an "act of war". President Donald Trump called for an increase in [sanctions against Iran](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States_sanctions_against_Iran "United States sanctions against Iran") opposing the strikes.<sup id="cite_ref-389"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Iran%E2%80%93Saudi_Arabia_proxy_conflict#cite_note-389">[389]</a></sup> President Trump approved the deployment of additional U.S. troops to Saudi Arabia and the [United Arab Emirates](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_Arab_Emirates "United Arab Emirates") following the attack on Saudi oil facilities that the United States blamed on Iran.<sup id="cite_ref-390"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Iran%E2%80%93Saudi_Arabia_proxy_conflict#cite_note-390">[390]</a></sup>

#### Jordan [edit](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Iran%E2%80%93Saudi_Arabia_proxy_conflict&action=edit&section=36 "Edit section: Jordan")

Jordan has historically been on the Saudi bloc despite its slight rivalry. Jordan and Iran have sour relations with each other.<sup id="cite_ref-391"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Iran%E2%80%93Saudi_Arabia_proxy_conflict#cite_note-391">[391]</a></sup>

### Other involved parties [edit](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Iran%E2%80%93Saudi_Arabia_proxy_conflict&action=edit&section=37 "Edit section: Other involved parties")

#### Turkey [edit](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Iran%E2%80%93Saudi_Arabia_proxy_conflict&action=edit&section=38 "Edit section: Turkey")

[Turkey](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Turkey "Turkey") has long seen Iran's expansions as threats but also perceived Saudi Arabia's influence with a similar reception, and is seeking to build itself as an alternative replacement to both Saudi and Iranian influences, to a degree.<sup id="cite_ref-392"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Iran%E2%80%93Saudi_Arabia_proxy_conflict#cite_note-392">[392]</a></sup>

However, the growing Turkish military, political, and economic expansions have caused some concern on the Saudi and Iranian sides. Iran considers Turkish military adventurism in Syria and its growing encounter against Iran in the Levant and Iraq as a challenge, not to mention its good relationship with [Azerbaijan](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Azerbaijan "Azerbaijan"), which is very antagonistic to Iran. Meanwhile, Saudi Arabia has also begun a systematic campaign to rewrite history, changing the Ottoman Caliphate into the occupier of Arabia; while it has also partially financed other megaprojects to counter the growing Turkish presence in Qatar, Sudan, Maghreb, Somalia, Kuwait, and Oman.<sup id="cite_ref-393"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Iran%E2%80%93Saudi_Arabia_proxy_conflict#cite_note-393">[393]</a></sup>

#### Qatar [edit](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Iran%E2%80%93Saudi_Arabia_proxy_conflict&action=edit&section=39 "Edit section: Qatar")

[Qatar–Saudi Arabia relations](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Foreign_relations_of_Saudi_Arabia#Qatar "Foreign relations of Saudi Arabia") have been strained since the beginning of the Arab Spring.<sup id="cite_ref-nbcnews_n768966_394-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Iran%E2%80%93Saudi_Arabia_proxy_conflict#cite_note-nbcnews_n768966-394">[394]</a></sup> Qatar has been a focus of controversy in the Saudi-Iranian rivalry due to Saudi Arabia's longstanding concern about the country's relationship with Iran and Iranian-backed militant groups.<sup id="cite_ref-The_Guardian_395-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Iran%E2%80%93Saudi_Arabia_proxy_conflict#cite_note-The_Guardian-395">[395]</a></sup>

In June 2017, Saudi Arabia, the United Arab Emirates, Bahrain, Egypt, the [Maldives](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Maldives "Maldives"), Mauritania, Sudan, Senegal, Djibouti, Comoros, Jordan, the Tobruk-based Libyan government, and the [Hadi](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Abdrabbuh_Mansur_Hadi "Abdrabbuh Mansur Hadi")\-led Yemeni government [severed diplomatic relations with Qatar](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/2017%E2%80%9319_Qatar_diplomatic_crisis "2017–19 Qatar diplomatic crisis") and blocked their airspace and sea routes, in addition to Saudi Arabia blocking the only land crossing. The reasons cited were Qatar's relations with Iran, [Al-Jazeera](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Al_Jazeera_Media_Network "Al Jazeera Media Network")'s coverage of other GCC states and Egypt, and Qatar's alleged [support of Islamist groups](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Qatar_and_state-sponsored_terrorism "Qatar and state-sponsored terrorism").<sup id="cite_ref-Associated_Press_396-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Iran%E2%80%93Saudi_Arabia_proxy_conflict#cite_note-Associated_Press-396">[396]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Reuters_397-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Iran%E2%80%93Saudi_Arabia_proxy_conflict#cite_note-Reuters-397">[397]</a></sup> Qatar was also expelled from the anti-[Houthi](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Houthi "Houthi") coalition.<sup id="cite_ref-bbc.com_398-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Iran%E2%80%93Saudi_Arabia_proxy_conflict#cite_note-bbc.com-398">[398]</a></sup> Qatar's defense minister Khalid bin Mohammed Al Attiyah called the blockade akin to a bloodless declaration of war, and Qatar's finance minister [Ali Sharif Al Emadi](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ali_Sharif_Al_Emadi "Ali Sharif Al Emadi") stated that Qatar was rich enough to withstand the blockade.<sup id="cite_ref-dohanews.co_399-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Iran%E2%80%93Saudi_Arabia_proxy_conflict#cite_note-dohanews.co-399">[399]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-money.cnn.com_400-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Iran%E2%80%93Saudi_Arabia_proxy_conflict#cite_note-money.cnn.com-400">[400]</a></sup> As of 2020, Saudi Arabia, the United Arab Emirates, Bahrain and Egypt have maintained the blockade, whereas all other countries mentioned above had rebuilt their relations with Qatar. The blockade ended in 2021 when the four countries and Qatar agreed to restore relations.<sup id="cite_ref-401"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Iran%E2%80%93Saudi_Arabia_proxy_conflict#cite_note-401">[401]</a></sup>

The bloc sought a guarantee that Qatar will in the future align in all matters with other Gulf states, discuss all of its decisions with them, and provide regular reports on its activity (monthly for the first year, quarterly for the second, and annually for the following ten years). They also demanded the deportation of all political refugees who live in Qatar to their countries of origin, freezing their assets, providing any desired information about their residency, movements, and finances, and revoking their Qatari citizenship if naturalized. They also demanded that Qatar be forbidden from granting citizenship to any additional fugitives.<sup id="cite_ref-The_Washington_Post_402-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Iran%E2%80%93Saudi_Arabia_proxy_conflict#cite_note-The_Washington_Post-402">[402]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-washingtonpost.com_403-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Iran%E2%80%93Saudi_Arabia_proxy_conflict#cite_note-washingtonpost.com-403">[403]</a></sup> Upon Qatar's rejection of these demands, the countries involved announced that the blockade would remain in place until Qatar changed its policies.<sup id="cite_ref-aljazeera.com_404-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Iran%E2%80%93Saudi_Arabia_proxy_conflict#cite_note-aljazeera.com-404">[404]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Saudi-led_group_vows_'appropriate'_405-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Iran%E2%80%93Saudi_Arabia_proxy_conflict#cite_note-Saudi-led_group_vows_'appropriate'-405">[405]</a></sup> On 24 August 2017, Qatar announced that they would restore full diplomatic relations with Iran.<sup id="cite_ref-ndtv.com_406-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Iran%E2%80%93Saudi_Arabia_proxy_conflict#cite_note-ndtv.com-406">[406]</a></sup>

Saudi Arabia together with the United Arab Emirates (UAE), Egypt and Bahrain, restored bilateral relations with Qatar on January 5, 2021. Diplomatic and trade ties were severed and a land, sea and air blocked on Qatar were imposed in June 2017.<sup id="cite_ref-407"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Iran%E2%80%93Saudi_Arabia_proxy_conflict#cite_note-407">[407]</a></sup>

Qatar also has a history of funding the [Houthi movement](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Houthi_movement "Houthi movement"), the [Muslim Brotherhood](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Muslim_Brotherhood "Muslim Brotherhood"), [Hezbollah](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hezbollah "Hezbollah"),<sup id="cite_ref-408"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Iran%E2%80%93Saudi_Arabia_proxy_conflict#cite_note-408">[408]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Weinthal_279-1"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Iran%E2%80%93Saudi_Arabia_proxy_conflict#cite_note-Weinthal-279">[279]</a></sup> the [Al-Ashtar Brigades](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Al-Ashtar_Brigades "Al-Ashtar Brigades"),<sup id="cite_ref-409"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Iran%E2%80%93Saudi_Arabia_proxy_conflict#cite_note-409">[409]</a></sup> and [al-Qaeda](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Al-Qaeda "Al-Qaeda").<sup id="cite_ref-410"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Iran%E2%80%93Saudi_Arabia_proxy_conflict#cite_note-410">[410]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-411"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Iran%E2%80%93Saudi_Arabia_proxy_conflict#cite_note-411">[411]</a></sup>

#### Russia [edit](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Iran%E2%80%93Saudi_Arabia_proxy_conflict&action=edit&section=40 "Edit section: Russia")

Russia has been aligned with Iran and Syria for years. It [intervened in Syria](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Russian_military_intervention_in_the_Syrian_Civil_War "Russian military intervention in the Syrian Civil War") to provide support for the Assad government and to target rebel groups, working together with Iran and using Iranian air bases to stage air strikes.<sup id="cite_ref-412"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Iran%E2%80%93Saudi_Arabia_proxy_conflict#cite_note-412">[412]</a></sup> It also joined Iran, Iraq, and Syria in forming a [joint intelligence-sharing coalition](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Russia%E2%80%93Syria%E2%80%93Iran%E2%80%93Iraq_coalition "Russia–Syria–Iran–Iraq coalition") as part of the fight against [ISIL](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/ISIL "ISIL").<sup id="cite_ref-413"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Iran%E2%80%93Saudi_Arabia_proxy_conflict#cite_note-413">[413]</a></sup> The alliance coincided with the [US-led coalition](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Combined_Joint_Task_Force_%E2%80%93_Operation_Inherent_Resolve "Combined Joint Task Force – Operation Inherent Resolve") created a year earlier to fight ISIL. The competing military actions were seen as part of a larger proxy conflict between the United States and Russia.<sup id="cite_ref-414"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Iran%E2%80%93Saudi_Arabia_proxy_conflict#cite_note-414">[414]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-415"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Iran%E2%80%93Saudi_Arabia_proxy_conflict#cite_note-415">[415]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-416"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Iran%E2%80%93Saudi_Arabia_proxy_conflict#cite_note-416">[416]</a></sup> However, Russia's tie with Saudi Arabia has become increasingly warmed since 2010s despite numerous differences, thus sometimes affected Iran's stance on relations with Russia.<sup id="cite_ref-417"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Iran%E2%80%93Saudi_Arabia_proxy_conflict#cite_note-417">[417]</a></sup>

In the past, Saudi Arabia backed Chechen and Dagestani fighters as well as [Arab Mujahedeen](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arab_Mujahideen_in_Chechnya "Arab Mujahideen in Chechnya") in the [North Caucasus](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/North_Caucasus "North Caucasus") during the First and Second Chechen Civil Wars in the 1990s, in which Russia has fought against them.<sup id="cite_ref-418"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Iran%E2%80%93Saudi_Arabia_proxy_conflict#cite_note-418">[418]</a></sup> In recent years however, Saudi Arabia has shifted its diplomacy to become friendlier to Russia, with [King Salman](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Salman_of_Saudi_Arabia "Salman of Saudi Arabia") became the first Saudi head of state to visit Russia, heralding possible political change.<sup id="cite_ref-419"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Iran%E2%80%93Saudi_Arabia_proxy_conflict#cite_note-419">[419]</a></sup> Since then, Saudi Arabia and Russia have started to support each other in various conflicts in Syria and Libya, with Saudi Arabia supported Russian intervention in Syria, while Russia and Saudi Arabia have together backed [Khalifa Haftar](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Khalifa_Haftar "Khalifa Haftar")'s forces in Libya.<sup id="cite_ref-420"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Iran%E2%80%93Saudi_Arabia_proxy_conflict#cite_note-420">[420]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-421"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Iran%E2%80%93Saudi_Arabia_proxy_conflict#cite_note-421">[421]</a></sup> In addition, Saudi Arabia and Russia are also becoming more antagonistic to Iranian ambitions in the Middle East, as revealed by their secret cooperation alongside Israel and Jordan against Iran.<sup id="cite_ref-hamodia_422-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Iran%E2%80%93Saudi_Arabia_proxy_conflict#cite_note-hamodia-422">[422]</a></sup>

Likewise, since late 2010s, sign of Iranian–Russian friction emerged, following Iran's attempt to turn Bashar al-Assad to align with the Islamist ideology of the Iranian regime which opposed to Russia's desire for a secular state.<sup id="cite_ref-423"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Iran%E2%80%93Saudi_Arabia_proxy_conflict#cite_note-423">[423]</a></sup> Russia's attitude toward Iran is also becoming more negative due to Iranian desire to control the Middle East, resulting in growing cooperation with Saudi Arabia.<sup id="cite_ref-hamodia_422-1"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Iran%E2%80%93Saudi_Arabia_proxy_conflict#cite_note-hamodia-422">[422]</a></sup>

#### Oman [edit](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Iran%E2%80%93Saudi_Arabia_proxy_conflict&action=edit&section=41 "Edit section: Oman")

[Oman](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Oman "Oman") is a member of the GCC and thus, maintains a close relationship with Saudi Arabia. However, unlike the majority of GCC countries, Oman does not perceive Iran as a threat. Oman has long promoted itself as the main stabilizing force amidst the intensified Iranian–Saudi conflict and often prefers a diplomatic solution to end the proxy wars.<sup id="cite_ref-424"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Iran%E2%80%93Saudi_Arabia_proxy_conflict#cite_note-424">[424]</a></sup> However, it is alleged of Houthi support and Iranian arms smuggling.<sup id="cite_ref-Oman's_dangerous_double_game_35-1"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Iran%E2%80%93Saudi_Arabia_proxy_conflict#cite_note-Oman's_dangerous_double_game-35">[35]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-watanserb.com_36-1"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Iran%E2%80%93Saudi_Arabia_proxy_conflict#cite_note-watanserb.com-36">[36]</a></sup>

#### Pakistan [edit](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Iran%E2%80%93Saudi_Arabia_proxy_conflict&action=edit&section=42 "Edit section: Pakistan")

Pakistan is a major partner of Saudi Arabia, but is also a neighbor of Iran, sharing historical ties as well. Prior to 1979, the three countries formed a moderate relationship and acted as responsible Muslim states. However, since 1979, Pakistan has fallen into sectarian discord due to growing attempt by Iran and Saudi Arabia to spread influence to the country, with Pakistan having a balance of Sunni and Shi'a Muslims.<sup id="cite_ref-425"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Iran%E2%80%93Saudi_Arabia_proxy_conflict#cite_note-425">[425]</a></sup>
